# PM Session Handoff

## 2026-07-18 (v33 beat 3 — **M9.7-W2 AUDIT: ACCEPT** · R1/R2 ratified · the S31-ROUTE watch · the core commit ordered · the Matter REC)

**The intake.** The Coder delivered M9.7-W2 on the working tree at `1aa809d` (18 porcelain entries, all integration-zigbee + MODULE_CONTEXT), full-bar: tests-first red-first staged honest (stage-A exactly 30 red, every one for the right reason), stage-B + fleet fixes **518/0/0 forced-fresh** (466 baseline + 52 new), full `./gradlew check` GREEN ×3 in-session, app **19/0/0** + lifecycle **56/0/0** forced-fresh (`RegistryApplyCensusTest` + arch rules hold), and Nick independently re-ran `clean.sh` + the module suite `--rerun-tasks` + full `check` — all GREEN. Zero mints (73/43/55), zero module-info/build/schema/public-surface diffs, frozen tokens untouched, `ReportingConfigurator` untouched.

**TWO-LAYER AUDIT: ACCEPT.** Layer-1: the Coder ran a 5-lens pre-write source-verification fleet — which caught, BEFORE any code existed, that `ZclCodec` sign-extends int16 (the temperature invalid sentinel is **−32768 post-decode**, never wire 0x8000; a test written from the instruction's framing would have enshrined the wrong constant and left a fabrication hole where a mis-typed uint16 0x8000 publishes 327.68 °C) — plus a 4-lens adversarial diff review; every finding closed in-session (two classifier mutation survivors gained killer tests; DP-2 gained `doesNotContain(0xFC37)`; the band guard closed the demonstrated hole). ## 2026-07-08 (v25 beat 4 — **M9.5-DUR LANDED `ef1d2c5` + CI GREEN ×2 (gate of record CLOSED)** · **DURb RULED (a) BEFORE-THE-SOAK, 5b-FIRST** (verbatim below) · **5b MID-FLIGHT: leg-1 + KEYb piggyback PROVEN; restart legs pend the log read** · two handoff gaps OWNED)

**THE DURb ROUTING RULING (Nick, 2026-07-08 — PRESERVE VERBATIM):** *"(a) — author now, land before the soak. One firm sequencing constraint: after iteration 5b. The decisive reason is a principle, not a preference: **you soak the code you ship.** The 72 h soak with NQ-6 is the durability certification — so the durability foundation must be final before it runs. Landing DURb after the soak means shipping a change to the identity path that the certification never exercised; you'd owe a re-soak or ship un-soaked durability code. That's exactly the asterisk you don't want on the one guarantee AMD-99 exists to make. And the flip side is the upside: NQ-6 is DURb's natural test bed — a restart spike is precisely what stresses the re-registration/re-link path, so landing before the soak means the soak validates the fix instead of running around it. The cost of doing it now is near-zero, which removes the only reason to defer: it's F1-clean — no new event type, no AMD, no governance latency — and it clears accumulated debt in one pass (the long-deferred BENCH-VERIFY javadoc flips, the permitJoinDeadline one-liner, the SD-3 fence polish, the apply-caller pin). Several of those matter during certification: the permitJoinDeadline clear and the reopen path get exercised in the acceptance P6 reopen leg and across soak restarts. So landing them before the soak means the whole certification chain runs on tidied code. The schedule pays for it — it's weeks to the go/no-go, and DURb is a KEYb-sized micro-WU. The one hard line: 5b first. 5b proves the DUR foundation clean on silicon (same IDs across restart, pin-2 re-link fires); don't stack the edge-fix on an unvalidated foundation, or a 5b surprise makes you debug DUR + DURb together. Preferred path: 5b → DURb → acceptance run → 72 h soak (both the acceptance evidence and the soak then certify final code). If you'd rather bank the acceptance-run milestone first, 5b → acceptance → DURb → soak is acceptable — the non-negotiable is simply that DURb lands before the soak, not during or after it."*

**THE RATIFICATION (Nick, 2026-07-08 — PRESERVED VERBATIM; the DP-18-C-class record):**

```markdown
Verdict: ratify as recommended — (A), and R‑B through R‑E as written.
This is the strongest work product the arc has produced, and it earns ratification cleanly. It doesn't just answer the five things I asked for at the checkpoint — it exceeds several of them, and it caught things I didn't ask for. I'll walk why it's sound, reframe what it actually buys us, then give the DUR coding WU its carry-list (none of which blocks ratification).

Why it's sound
R‑A is decided on exactly the right criterion, and the rejection of (B) is airtight. (B) fails because its rebuild depends on zigbee-devices.json + profile files — non-log artifacts that can drift, lag, or be deleted — so the projection wouldn't be a pure function of replay. That's precisely the disqualifier. And the denormalization note (§2) is the sharpest line in the document: storing capability schemas in the event isn't waste, it's recording what was installed at adoption, including the DP‑a confirmation tuning — the fact a trust product must be able to prove later, independent of what a profile file says today. That's not a workaround; it's event-sourcing done correctly.
R‑B ships the invariant with teeth and reasons correctly about the reach subtlety. REG‑INV‑1 + the REGISTRY_MUTATION_ONLY_VIA_PROJECTION ArchUnit rule landing in the DUR WU, no N‑2 deferral — exactly what I demanded. And §4's handling of the 2026‑06‑13 enforcement-reach caveat is correct: that caveat is about non‑app test code; this rule targets production code, which app's test classpath catches across every module. Whoever wrote this understood the trap and stepped around it.

R‑C is the P1 boundedness proof I wanted — a registry-projection subscriber on the existing bus replay machinery, Phase‑3 CORE_DOMAIN, riding the existing Phase‑3‑before‑Phase‑6 catch-up invariant, with exactly ONE sanctioned addition (a composition-root await) and a STOP on anything wider. The fallback (direct ordered store read) is named as coder latitude. Bounded, existing-seam, flagged.

The correctness detail that shows real care: the write-ahead + idempotent-by-identity apply (REG‑INV‑1) means adoption still populates the registry synchronously — the event is durable, then applied inline, and the later bus delivery is a no-op. So there's no async gap at adoption; entities stay immediately usable. That's the subtle thing a weaker version would have broken.
R‑D (tombstone vs one-time bench wipe, cleanly separated, additive/no-migration) and R‑E (mints explicit — and it caught the EventCategoryMapping +2 easy-miss and the AllEventClasses aggregators, plus the register deltas 174→175 / 52→53) are both exactly right.

What this actually buys us — reframe
This isn't a bug fix with a governance cost. Ratifying (A) extends the moat itself: the event log now carries full device provenance — what was adopted, as what, with which capabilities and confirmation tuning, and when — replayable and immutable. For a product whose entire pitch is the honest, single, replayable log, closing "the one place everything-is-derived-from-the-log had a hole" (§1) makes the moat more complete, not just patched. That's why doing (i) instead of the snapshot was the right call, and the AMD proves it was affordable.

Carry-list for the DUR coding WU (not ratification blockers)

The refactor scope is ALL registry mutators, not just adopt()'s — §8's phrasing ("the single-apply-path refactor of adopt()'s registry writes") slightly undersells it. The whole point of the ArchUnit rule is that nothing outside the projection mutates the registries. The grounding survey must enumerate every current mutator before the refactor — including the M9.4a pin‑2 relink path's updateEntity and any availability/update writes — and route or retire each. Likely resolution: pin‑2's re-install of confirmation overrides becomes redundant post‑DUR (the tuning now persists via replay) and is removed; a genuine capability change (Q10 re-interview) rides an idempotent re-emit of entity_registered, not a third event type. The rule will catch any missed mutator, which is good — but if the survey finds many, that's the G2 sizing signal to flag before dispatch.

The capability-mirror layer is the WU's largest chunk and where G2 risk concentrates. Mirroring the full attribute/command/confirmation schema forest into event-model-local records, both directions (emit + apply), under the "full-fidelity, no silent drops" STOP gate. This is bounded but it's the part most likely to cascade — watch it specifically, and add a MODULE_CONTEXT gotcha that the mirrors must track the device-model schema (a new schema field needs a mirror field or an explicit exclusion ruling).

The intra‑Phase‑3 ordering is the load-bearing seam — the registry projection must be caught up to log head before automation definitions bind entity refs, not just before Phase 6. §5's "one flagged await" is the right sanctioned fix; the survey just has to prove the exact hook exists or add the single await.
Test device_removed even though nothing emits it yet — feed the projection the tombstone and assert the device+entities drop, so the mechanism is proven complete though unexercised in production.

Two optional tightenings (fold before ratifying, or leave to the WU — your call):

1. One line that registration updates ride idempotent re-emit of the existing two types — no third event type — so the +2 mint is closed and can't be silently reopened later. (REG‑INV‑1's idempotency clause implies it; making it explicit locks the count.)
2. A half-line precision on §6/§8: durable IDs fix the restart-orphan class specifically; the removal→state‑view cleanup rides the future removal-emission milestone (correctly out of scope now — just don't let "fixes orphan accumulation" read as fixing the removal class too).
```

## 2026-07-08 (v24 beat 4 — **THE TWO RULINGS BEAT: DUR = (i) EVENT-SOURCE THE REGISTRIES (ruled, verbatim below, with two guardrails) · §B GO → M9.4-KEYb AUTHORED ISSUE-READY — DISPATCH AT WILL** · the completing survey: **BOUNDED CONFIRMED** (~2 event types hold; one payload fork rides the AMD) · beat-3 landed: bench `aa45edc` 1-exact · hivemind `2408995` 2-exact)

**THE DUR RULING (Nick, 2026-07-08 — PRESERVE VERBATIM; the DP-18-C-class record):** *"DUR — (i). Event-source the registries."* His four reasons: (1) *"The moat is the single event-sourced log. Imperative in-memory registries that aren't derived from it are the one place the 'everything is provably derived from the log' claim has a hole — and for a trust-in-the-log product, that hole is exactly what the north star says to close before freeze. (ii)'s snapshot doesn't close it; it bolts a second, drift-prone source of truth onto the moat — the precise asterisk we don't want to ship."* (2) *"It's a one-way door being frozen at V1. The event model is the hardest thing to change post-launch, and `confirmation[]` is the precedent: we amend the model for load-bearing moat pieces. Cheaper now than after freeze."* (3) *"The schedule pays for the correctness. The join arc closed weeks early; it's ~5–6 weeks to the go/no-go. So (i)'s cost over (ii) is essentially zero in schedule — which is the only thing (ii) was buying."* (4) *"(i) fixes four things root-cause: durable identity, the orphan rows, a real `device_removed` tombstone, and pin-2 across restart. (ii) fixes only the first and adds a new drift surface."* **TWO GUARDRAILS (binding on the hub):** (G1) *"Govern it like `confirmation[]`. Ratify the record shapes and the invariant that the device/entity registries are projections of the log (so it can never silently regress) in the design/AMD layer before the coding WU."* (G2) *"Bound it — watch the P1 sizing smell. Minimal surface: the event(s) carrying the full device + entity records, a boot projection rebuild, orphan tombstoning — not a general registry rearchitecture. If the completing survey shows materially more than ~2 event types or a cascade of amendments, flag it before you commit."* **And his sequencing insight, on the record:** *"automations load only at boot, and boot re-mints identity, so an entity-bound automation can never survive the very restart that loads it. Durable identity is a hard prerequisite for the hero loop, not just the soak's restart leg."*

**The completing survey (read-only, at `8800424`) — GUARDRAIL-2 VERDICT: BOUNDED CONFIRMED.** Two event types hold (device-registration + entity-registration class); `device_removed` ALREADY EXISTS as an event type with a codec/category mapping and ZERO production emitters — tombstoning gives it its first real semantics, no new type. Record shapes at source: `Device` = 14 components (identity wrappers + Strings + collections + Instant — payload-friendly); `Entity` = 12 components INCLUDING `List<CapabilityInstance>`, and `CapabilityInstance` is a DEEP structure (attribute/command schema maps + `ConfirmationPolicy`). **The one design fork the AMD must rule (JPMS-forced):** an event record in `com.homesynapse.event` can NEVER reference device-model types (the payload-residency rule — device requires event, so event→device is the AMD-52 cycle class). So: **(A) flattened-full-record payloads** (the all-String/leaf-value idiom over the whole Device+Entity forest incl. capabilities — pure log projection, heavy schema) vs **(B) identity-binding payloads** (deviceId/entityIds-by-endpoint/IEEE/integrationId/matchedProfileId/slugs — flat, light) **+ deterministic capability re-derivation at boot** through the SAME classification+installOverrides path adoption uses, sourced from the already-persisted `zigbee-devices.json` cache (survey-confirmed: it persists NodeDescriptor + endpoints + manufacturer/model + interviewStatus + matchedProfileId — everything but the minted IDs, which is exactly the gap). Hub lean: (B) — lighter, JPMS-clean, and the invariant wording then reads "registry IDENTITY is a pure projection of the log; characterization re-derives deterministically" — but (A) is the purer reading of G1's invariant; **the AMD presents both, Nick ratifies.** Also found: the adoption slice already has a device-restore seam shape (`:380` region puts into `devicesByIeee` from an existing `Device`) — the rebuild has a natural landing. Boot seam: registries install at Phase 3.1; integrations launch at Phase 6 — the rebuild sits between. Existing stored `device_adopted` events are untouched (codecs are per-type; no migration).

**§B → M9.4-KEYb AUTHORED ISSUE-READY** (`context/instructions/2026-07-08_M9.4-KEYb_key-establishment-progress-reclassification_coding-instruction.md`): `KeyEstablishment.progress()` = exactly {0x06,0x07,0x0C} (the ruled set) → the middle DEBUG arm `zigbee.key_establishment_progress` in `handleKeyEstablishment`; `established()` + `statusName()` + both frozen tokens BYTE-UNTOUCHED; THE PIN re-asserted in every new test; T-KB1 (the healthy 0x06→0x34 sequence → exactly one INFO, zero WARN) / T-KB2 (each progress byte → DEBUG) / T-KB3 (0x11 + 0x33 still WARN — the regression pin) / T-KB4 (the truth table); DEBUG-capture watch-out named (vacuous-VERIFY class); 4 files, zero mints/surface; G-KB1–5. Silicon confirmation piggybacks on the next fresh join — no dedicated iteration.

**DUR ruling — SHARPENED by the grounding survey (this is why we verify before authoring):** the registries are **imperative in-memory, NOT event-sourced** — `DeviceAdoptedEvent` carries ONLY `entityId` (no device record, no capabilities, no bindings); there is NO `entity_registered`/`device_registered` event type; `adopt()` populates `deviceRegistry.createDevice` + `entityRegistry.createEntity` + the IEEE→id/binding maps imperatively from live interview data that is never persisted as an event. So **option (i) "event-replay rehydration at boot" means first making the registries PROJECTIONS of the log — minting proper registration events (device_registered + entity_registered carrying the full records) + a boot rebuild** — the architecturally-correct, event-sourced-native answer (and the root fix: the registries SHOULD be projections), but a **governance-class WU** (new event types → schema → codec → the 71/41/53 mint pins → the adoption path emits them). **Option (ii) persisted registry snapshot** avoids the event-schema change but bolts on a PARALLEL truth artifact (drift-prone, against the event-sourced grain) — faster to the soak. **(iii) cache-side re-link** stays insufficient alone. **Hub REC: (i)** — the registries-as-projections is the design, this is a one-way-door foundation worth getting right, and the window (~Aug 16) has room for a bounded governance WU; **(ii) if velocity-to-soak outranks architecture-purity here** (your call — it's a genuine fork, both now grounded). #### OR-APP-AUTH — Unauthenticated composition-root HTTP surface (core-review C1 / B-H1) — [✅ RESOLVED-for-REST 2026-06-20] (NEW 2026-06-18)
- **RESOLVED 2026-06-20 (AB-1; `./gradlew check` GREEN 149; PM WUCP Phase 2 APPROVE):** the REST surface is authenticated — `StandardAuthMiddleware`/`StandardRateLimiter` wired via a catch-all `installAuth` over `/api/*`+`/internal/*` (auth-before-canonicalize, RFC 9457), loopback-default bind (`HomeSynapseConfig.bindHost`), first-run pairing token → `config/initial_api_token`. INV-SE-02 now has enforcing code + tests for the REST interface. **Carried forward:** WS first-message auth is an acceptance gate on the **new WS Phase-3 runtime + auth WU** (`api.ws` was Phase-2 scaffold — no live WS surface today; the shared `OpaqueTokenStore`/`AuthMiddleware` are built for it).
- **Status (2026-06-18):** OPEN — surfaced by the 2026-06-15 core-review (source-verified). The composition root (`lifecycle/.../HomeSynapseCore.java:408-435`) installs only `RestFilters.installReadinessGate` and calls `app.start(config.httpPort())` with **no `.host()`, no auth, no rate-limit**; `/internal/*` admin endpoints sit outside even the readiness gate. **INV-SE-02 ("auth mandatory on every external interface; no local-trust exception") has no enforcing implementation** — `AuthMiddleware`/`RateLimiter` are zero-impl. Latent only because `main()` is a stub.
- **Severity:** HIGH (security). The moment app-bootstrap wires `main()`, this is a live unauthenticated surface.
- **Owner:** Nick (bind-posture decision: loopback-default vs all-interfaces — feeds the CC-1 spike) / PM (coding instruction) / Coder (implement at app-bootstrap). **Resolution condition:** the app-bootstrap milestone ships `AuthMiddleware before("/api/*")` + `RateLimiter` + a decided bind posture, with auth-before-network-exposure tracked as a gate. Closed when INV-SE-02 has enforcing code + tests and app-bootstrap lands GREEN.

#### OR-RF-DECRYPT — Read-path decrypt failure aborts the whole replay (core-review C2 / F-A1) — [✅ RESOLVED-at-MVP 2026-06-20] (NEW 2026-06-18)
- **RESOLVED-at-MVP 2026-06-20 (AB-2; GREEN; PM WUCP Phase 2 APPROVE):** the read path now fails **closed** with a distinct typed `PayloadDecryptionException` (per-read-batch scope, CASE-a key-absent / CASE-b GCM-auth) — the A3-ruled MVP posture; no more raw untyped whole-replay abort. **Carried forward:** the graceful per-row degrade *behavior* (`DegradedEvent`) is designed-not-wired (F4) and ships with the **crypto-shred WU** (gated on `chain_hash` liveness, ZERO today).
- **Status (2026-06-18):** OPEN — source-verified at the core-review (`core/persistence/.../SqliteEventStore.java:804-810` + `:896-913`). `fromRow` routes any `dek_ref`-bearing row through `decryptStoredPayload`, which **throws** on missing cipher, malformed `dek_ref`, GCM auth-fail, or a destroyed key. **No per-row catch → one bad row fails the whole `readRows` batch** — deliberately unlike codec parse failures, which degrade to `DegradedEvent` so the read continues. Consequences: a lost/corrupt `.root-key` → the **entire store is unreplayable** (vs INV-RF-04); when crypto-shred lands, replay across a shredded event throws (vs INV-PD-07). The missing-cipher-on-read and shredded-key-on-read paths have **no test**.
- **Severity:** HIGH (correctness/security, forward). Inert until `main()` activates `payloadCipher`; then it becomes a confidentiality-vs-availability contract gap that also blocks the crypto-shred differentiator.
- **Owner:** Nick (the confidentiality-vs-availability design tradeoff) / PM (coding instruction) / Coder (crypto-shred WU). **Resolution condition:** decide the contract **before** crypto-shred is built — most likely catch decrypt failure in `fromRow` and emit `DegradedEvent` for the shredded/undecryptable case, keeping a hard fail only for "cipher entirely unwired but encrypted rows exist"; add tests for both read-side failure modes. Interlocks with OR-M6-NONCE restore-half (R-α) + the key-portability brief. Carry under the app-bootstrap lane.

#### OR-M6-NONCE — Counter-nonce crash/restore durability — [CLOSED 2026-06-19 — crash-half M6.3, restore-half AMD-94] (NEW 2026-06-07; carried from Doc 15 §6 at Lock)
- **Status (2026-06-19 — CLOSED):** both halves discharged. **Crash-half** = M6.3 durable, fsync-ahead-of-return per-scope counter (GREEN `1eddd9a`). **Restore-half** = **AMD-94 RATIFIED + folded into Locked Doc 15 2026-06-19** (rotate-DEK-on-restore = additive new DEK version, retain priors; carry-high-water-mark demoted to a defense-in-depth cross-check; the fail-closed boot invariant REC-235). Per the ratified DOCS-review edit **E-1**, the boot invariant is discharged after a restore **only** by installing a fresh DEK version — rotation is the restore-completion gate; the counter-proven-≥-all-priors branch is the crash-recovery path (sound because the M6.3 counter is durable), and must not clear a restore (a restore can roll the counter back below a used nonce and erase the true-high-water evidence). AMD-94-INV-01 (`Architecture_Invariants_v1.md` §48) discharges the AMD-86-INV-01 (§35) restore-half corollary. The §6 `[BLOCKING-for-M6-impl]` marker is resolved. Mechanics ship at the future backup/restore WU; the boot invariant rides app-bootstrap AB-2. _Prior status history follows._
- **Status (2026-06-13 — M6.3 landed GREEN, PM WUCP Phase 2 APPROVE):** the write-path half (a) is **DISCHARGED** — M6.3 ships the config-side durable per-scope nonce counter (`scope_nonce_counters.json`, fsync-ahead-of-return inside the `ScopeKeyManager` lock, re-init from the persisted max on boot — never from memory), and the Doc 15 §13.4 kill-mid-encrypt nonce-monotonicity test (`AtRestEncryptionWritePathTest.killMidEncryptThenRestart_nonceNeverRepeats`) is GREEN in the full `./gradlew check` (147 tasks). The restore half (b) **remains OPEN**, re-homed to side-research **R-α** (crash-safe backup/restore for an event-sourced + per-scope-encrypted store): M6.3 only "does not preclude" DEK-rotation-on-restore (instruction DP-D); the full backup/restore co-design (foundation-readiness F3) carries the remaining obligation.
- **Severity:** HIGH for the M6 at-rest-encryption implementation (a cryptographic-correctness gate — catastrophic if missed). NOT a blocker for Doc 15's Lock: the review (J6/J7) correctly classified it as blocking the M6 *implementation*, not the *design*. Logged here so it is not lost now that Doc 15 is Locked (the explicit M6 carry the brief required).
- **Detail:** Doc 15 §3.4 mandates counter-based deterministic 96-bit GCM nonces per scope (never random — to avoid the GCM birthday bound). If the per-scope nonce counter repeats after a crash, **or** a restored backup reintroduces a counter value already used under the same DEK, then (key, nonce) reuse **breaks AES-256-GCM confidentiality AND authentication** for that scope (the catastrophic GCM nonce-reuse failure). Documented in Doc 15 §6 (Failure Modes — "Counter-nonce reuse across crash/restore"), §13.4 (Testing Strategy), and the §16 summary; it is the AMD-86-INV-01 corollary registered in `Architecture_Invariants_v1.md` §35.
- **Owner:** PM (embed verbatim in the M6 coding instruction) / Coder (implement at M6). **Resolution condition:** the M6 at-rest-encryption WU (a) persists the per-scope counter high-water mark atomically with (or ahead of) the encrypted write and re-inits from the persisted max on boot — never from memory; and (b) co-designs the deferred backup/restore feature (foundation-readiness F3) so a restore can never resume a scope at a counter ≤ any value already used under that DEK (rotate the DEK on restore, or carry the high-water mark in the backup). Closed when the M6 impl ships with the §13.4 kill-mid-encrypt nonce-monotonicity test GREEN.

#### OR-M13-SDNOTIFY — sd_notify real AF_UNIX-datagram transport deferred to M13 (NEW 2026-06-07)
- **Severity:** LOW–MEDIUM (a *functional* Tier-1 systemd health reporter needs it; M5-A ships the contract + protocol semantics correctly behind a seam — compile + unit tests GREEN; no MVP consumer is blocked until on-device Tier-1 deployment).
- **Detail:** Pure OpenJDK 21 does not support AF_UNIX `SOCK_DGRAM` — `DatagramChannel.open(StandardProtocolFamily.UNIX)` throws `UnsupportedOperationException` at runtime (JEP 380 delivered Unix-domain *stream* sockets only). `sd_notify` is a datagram protocol, so `SystemdHealthReporter`'s real transport is non-functional on a stock JDK. M5-A isolates this behind the package-private `NotifyTransport` seam (the real transport is never constructed in tests; its default ctor now throws a clear "deferred to M13" `IllegalStateException`).
- **Owner:** PM (decide mechanism) / Coder (implement at M13 composition root). **Resolution condition:** pick the transport mechanism — **JNR/JNA native binding** (needs a version-catalog entry + approval; interacts with the GraalVM native-image decision) **vs a `systemd-notify` subprocess fallback** (watchdog-PID caveats; process-per-heartbeat is poor on a Pi) — **resolved with the M5-D evidence** (the choice is entangled with the native-image spike), then implemented at M13 where the reporter is constructed and `$NOTIFY_SOCKET` resolved. Closed when a working transport ships + a Tier-1 sd_notify integration test passes on-device.
- **M5-D decision matrix AUTHORED 2026-06-07** (`context/assessments/2026-06-07_M5-D_sd_notify_transport_decision_matrix_OR-M13-SDNOTIFY.md`): compares JNR/JNA vs the `systemd-notify` subprocess (+ the FFM/Panama JDK-native option due-diligence adds, + the M5-A "keep the seam, defer" baseline) with the GraalVM native-image entanglement flagged (cites the language-replatform assessment §1.2/§3.1/§4.1). **PM recommendation:** **defer the final commit to M13, gated on the M5-D GraalVM spike + the WatchdogSec decision + the JDK-version trajectory** — **reject JNR/JNA** (dominated: new dep + worst native-image fit for a 3-syscall job); **subprocess if no WATCHDOG keepalives** (zero-dep, closed-world-clean), else **FFM/Panama** (zero-dep, in-process, native-image-friendly; needs JDK 22+ / `--enable-preview`). **No catalog dependency added now.** Two items surfaced for Nick: (i) the GraalVM C15 spike should report whether JNR/JNA-class reflection bindings survive its closed-world config; (ii) **decide whether HomeSynapse opts into the systemd watchdog (WatchdogSec)** — a Doc 12 lifecycle choice that largely settles FFM-vs-subprocess.
